<p><b>Milton Keynes</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/55/En-uk-MiltonKeynes.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" data-file-height="11" data-file-width="11" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-MiltonKeynes.ogg" title="File:En-uk-MiltonKeynes.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ən/ 'on' in 'button'">ən</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'z' in 'Zion'">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>mil-tən-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">KEENZ</span></span></b></i></a></span>), locally abbreviated to <b>MK</b>, is a large town<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[note 1]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. It is the administrative centre of the <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Borough of Milton Keynes</a> and was formally designated as a <a href="/wiki/New_towns_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="New towns in the United Kingdom">new town</a> on 23 January 1967,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-longaz_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-longaz-3">[2]</a></sup> with the design brief to become a "city" in scale. It is located about 45 miles (72 km) north-west of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.</p>
<p>At designation, its 89 km<sup>2</sup> (34 sq mi) area incorporated the existing towns of <a href="/wiki/Bletchley" title="Bletchley">Bletchley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolverton" title="Wolverton">Wolverton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stony_Stratford" title="Stony Stratford">Stony Stratford</a>, along with another fifteen villages and farmland in between. It took its name from the existing <a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Middleton, Milton Keynes">village of Milton Keynes</a>, a few miles east of <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">the planned centre</a>.</p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 census</a>, the population of the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_urban_area" title="Milton Keynes urban area">Milton Keynes urban area</a>, including the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Newport_Pagnell" title="Newport Pagnell">Newport Pagnell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woburn_Sands" title="Woburn Sands">Woburn Sands</a>, was 229,941,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BUA_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-1">[1]</a></sup> and that of the wider borough, which has been a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> independent of Buckinghamshire County Council since 1997, was 248,800,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> compared with a population of around 53,000 for the same area in 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vision_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-vision-5">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Milton_Keynes" title="History of Milton Keynes">History of Milton Keynes</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_a_.22New_City.22">Birth of a "New City"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title='Edit section: Birth of a "New City"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1960s, the British government decided that a further generation of <a href="/wiki/New_towns_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="New towns in the United Kingdom">new towns</a> in the south-east of England was needed to relieve housing congestion in London.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="795" data-file-width="1270" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png/220px-BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png/330px-BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png/440px-BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BofMiltonKeynesUA-popn.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population trend of Borough and Urban Area 1801–2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the 1950s, <a href="/wiki/London_overspill" title="London overspill">overspill</a> housing for several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_borough" title="London borough">London boroughs</a> had been constructed in <a href="/wiki/Bletchley" title="Bletchley">Bletchley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clutch1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-clutch1-6">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clutch2_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-clutch2-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times1_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-times1-8">[7]</a></sup> Further studies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ses1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ses1-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times2_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-times2-10">[9]</a></sup> in the 1960s identified north Buckinghamshire as a possible site for a large new town, a new city,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planformk_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-planformk-11">[10]</a></sup> encompassing the existing towns of Bletchley, <a href="/wiki/Stony_Stratford" title="Stony Stratford">Stony Stratford</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wolverton,_Buckinghamshire" title="Wolverton, Buckinghamshire">Wolverton</a>. The New Town (informally and in planning documents, "New City") was to be the biggest yet, with a target population of 250,000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times3_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-times3-12">[11]</a></sup> in a "designated area" of 21,850 acres (34.1 sq mi; 88.4 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> The name "Milton Keynes" was taken from the existing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middleton_(Milton_Keynes_Village)" title="Middleton (Milton Keynes Village)">village of Milton Keynes</a> on the site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-llewelyn-david_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-llewelyn-david-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 January 1967 when the formal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_town" title="New town">new town</a> designation order was made,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-longaz_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-longaz-3">[2]</a></sup> the area to be developed was largely farmland and undeveloped villages. The site was deliberately located equidistant from London, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a> with the intention<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ses2_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-ses2-15">[14]</a></sup> that it would be self-sustaining and eventually become a major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_centre" title="Regional centre">regional centre</a> in its own right. Planning control was taken from elected <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local authorities</a> and delegated to the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Development_Corporation" title="Milton Keynes Development Corporation">Milton Keynes Development Corporation</a> (MKDC). Before construction began, every area was subject to detailed archaeological investigation: doing so has exposed a rich history of human settlement since <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> times and has provided a unique insight into the history of a large sample of the landscape of north <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a>.</p>
<p>The Corporation's strongly <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist</a> designs featured regularly in the magazines <i><a href="/wiki/Architectural_Design" title="Architectural Design">Architectural Design</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Architects%27_Journal" title="Architects' Journal">Architects' Journal</a></i>. MKDC was determined to learn from the mistakes made in the earlier <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Towns" title="New Towns">New Towns</a> and revisit the <a href="/wiki/Garden_city_movement" title="Garden city movement">Garden City ideals</a>. They set in place the characteristic <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_grid_road_system" title="Milton Keynes grid road system">grid roads</a> that run between districts (<a href="#Grid_roads_and_grid_squares">'grid squares'</a>), as well as the intensive planting, lakes and parkland that are so evident today. While still on the drawing board, planners noticed that the main streets near <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">the proposed city centre</a> would almost frame the rising sun on Midsummer's Day. Greenwich Observatory was consulted to obtain the exact angle required at the latitude of <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">Central Milton Keynes</a>, and they managed to persuade the engineers to shift the grid of roads a few degrees in response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">CMK</a> was not intended to be a traditional <a href="/wiki/Town_centre" title="Town centre">town centre</a> but a <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business and shopping district</a> to supplement Local Centres in most of the grid squares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-llewelyn-david_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-llewelyn-david-14">[13]</a></sup> This non-hierarchical devolved city plan was a departure from the English New Towns tradition and envisaged a wide range of industry and diversity of housing styles and tenures across the city. The largest and almost the last of the British New Towns, Milton Keynes has 'stood the test of time far better than most, and has proved flexible and adaptable'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bishop1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-bishop1-17">[16]</a></sup> The radical grid plan was inspired by the work of Californian urban theorist <a href="/wiki/Melvin_M._Webber" title="Melvin M. Webber">Melvin M. Webber</a> (1921–2006), described by the founding architect of Milton Keynes, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Walker" title="Derek Walker">Derek Walker</a> (1929-2015), as the "father of the city".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-walker2-18">[17]</a></sup> Webber thought that telecommunications meant that the old idea of a city as a concentric cluster was out of date and that cities which enabled people to travel around them readily would be the thing of the future achieving "community without <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/propinquity" title="wiktionary:propinquity">propinquity</a>" for residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webber_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-webber-19">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Government wound up MKDC in 1992, 25 years after the new town was founded, transferring control to the Commission for New Towns (CNT) and then finally to <a href="/wiki/English_Partnerships" title="English Partnerships">English Partnerships</a>, with the planning function returning to local council control (since 1974 and the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a>, the Borough of Milton Keynes). From 2004 to 2011 a Government <a href="/wiki/Quango" title="Quango">quango</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Partnership" title="Milton Keynes Partnership">Milton Keynes Partnership</a>, had development control powers to accelerate the growth of Milton Keynes.</p>
<p>Along with many other towns and boroughs, Milton Keynes competed for <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">formal city status</a> in the 2000, 2002 and 2012 competitions, but was not successful. Nevertheless, the term "city" is used by its citizens, local media and bus services to describe itself, perhaps because the term "town" is taken to mean one of the constituent towns. Road signs refer to "Central Milton Keynes" or "Shopping" when directing traffic to its centre.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prior_history">Prior history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prior history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG/170px-MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG/255px-MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG/340px-MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MiltonKeynesHoard.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reproductions of the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Hoard" title="Milton Keynes Hoard">Milton Keynes Hoard</a> (<a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Museum" title="Milton Keynes Museum">Milton Keynes Museum</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The area that was to become Milton Keynes encompassed a landscape that has a rich historic legacy. The area to be developed was largely farmland and undeveloped villages, but with evidence of permanent settlement dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. Before construction began, every area was subject to detailed archaeological investigation: doing so has provided a unique insight into the history of a large sample of the landscape of south-central England. There is evidence of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romano-British" title="Romano-British">Romano-British</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Norman" title="Anglo-Norman">Anglo-Norman</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">Medieval</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">Industrial revolution</a> settlements. Collections<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Oral_history" title="Oral history">oral history</a> covering the 20th century completes a picture that is described in detail in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Milton_Keynes" title="History of Milton Keynes">another article</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a>, the site of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> British codebreaking and <a href="/wiki/Colossus_computer" title="Colossus computer">Colossus</a>, the world's first programmable electronic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_computer" title="Digital computer">digital computer</a>, is a major component of MK's modern history. It is now a flourishing heritage attraction, receiving hundreds of thousands of visitors annually. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the boundary of Milton Keynes was defined in 1967, some 40,000 people<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-22">[21]</a></sup> lived in three towns and fifteen villages or hamlets in the "designated area" of 21,863 acres (8,848 ha).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_design">Urban design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Urban design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><i>The concepts that heavily influenced the design of the town are described in detail in article <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a> –  see 'cells' under <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning#Planning_and_aesthetics" title="Urban planning">Planning and aesthetics</a> (referring to grid squares). See also article <a href="/wiki/Single-use_zoning" title="Single-use zoning">single-use zoning</a>.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>Since the radical plan form and large scale of Milton Keynes attracted international attention, early phases of development include work by celebrated architects, including <a href="/wiki/Richard_MacCormac" title="Richard MacCormac">Sir Richard MacCormac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster,_Baron_Foster_of_Thames_Bank" title="Norman Foster, Baron Foster of Thames Bank">Lord Norman Foster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henning_Larsen" title="Henning Larsen">Henning Larsen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Erskine_(architect)" title="Ralph Erskine (architect)">Ralph Erskine</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Winter_(architect)" title="John Winter (architect)">John Winter</a>, and Martin Richardson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bishop2_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-bishop2-23">[22]</a></sup> Led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Campbell_of_Eskan" title="Lord Campbell of Eskan">Lord Campbell of Eskan</a> (Chairman) and <a href="/wiki/Fred_Roche" title="Fred Roche">Fred Roche</a> (General Manager), the Corporation attracted talented young architects led by the young and charismatic Derek Walker. In the modernist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mies_van_der_Rohe" title="Mies van der Rohe">Miesian</a> tradition is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Shopping_Centre" title="Milton Keynes Shopping Centre">Shopping Building</a> designed by Stuart Mosscrop and Christopher Woodward, a grade II <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a>, which the <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_Century_Society" title="Twentieth Century Society">Twentieth Century Society</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter_alia" title="Inter alia">inter alia</a></i> regards as the 'most distinguished' twentieth century retail building in Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> The contextual tradition that ran alongside it is exemplified by the Corporation's infill scheme at Cofferidge Close, Stony Stratford, designed by <a href="/wiki/Wayland_Tunley" title="Wayland Tunley">Wayland Tunley</a>, which carefully inserts into a historic stretch of High Street a modern retail facility, offices and <a href="/wiki/Parking_lot" title="Parking lot">car park</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Development_Corporation" title="Development Corporation">Development Corporation</a> also led an ambitious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_in_Milton_Keynes#Public_art" title="Art in Milton Keynes">Public art</a> programme.</p>
<p>The urban design has not been universally praised, however. Francis Tibbalds, president of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Town_Planning_Institute" title="Royal Town Planning Institute">Royal Town Planning Institute</a>, described the centre of Milton Keynes as "bland, rigid, sterile, and totally boring."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grid_roads_and_grid_squares">Grid roads and grid squares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Grid roads and grid squares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:33%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>The geography of Milton Keynes –  <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">the railway line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watling_Street" title="Watling Street">Watling Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Canal" title="Grand Union Canal">Grand Union Canal</a>, <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a> –  sets up a very strong north-south axis. If you've got to build a city between (them) it is very natural to take a pen and draw the rungs of a ladder. Ten miles by six is the size of this city –  22,000 acres. Do you lay it out like an American city, rigid orthogonal from side to side? Being more sensitive in 1966-7, the designers decided that the grid concept should apply but should be a lazy grid following the flow of land, its valleys, its ebbs and flows. That would be nicer to look at, more economical and efficient to build, and would sit more beautifully as a landscape intervention.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Professor David Lock, CBE<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></cite></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_grid_road_system" title="Milton Keynes grid road system">Milton Keynes grid road system</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_in_Milton_Keynes" title="List of districts in Milton Keynes">List of districts in Milton Keynes</a></div>
<p>The Milton Keynes Development Corporation planned the major road layout according to <a href="/wiki/Street_hierarchy" title="Street hierarchy">street hierarchy</a> principles, using a <a href="/wiki/Grid_plan" title="Grid plan">grid pattern</a> of approximately 1 km (0.62 mi) intervals, rather than on the more conventional <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/radial" title="wikt:radial">radial</a> pattern found in older settlements. Major internal roads run between communities, rather than through them: these distributor roads are known locally as <i><a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_grid_road_system" title="Milton Keynes grid road system">grid roads</a></i> and the spaces between them –  the districts –  are known as <i>grid squares</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Intervals of 1 km (0.62 mi) were chosen so that people would always be within walking distance of a bus stop. Consequently, each grid square is a semi-autonomous community, making a unique collective of 100 clearly identifiable neighbourhoods within the overall urban environment. The grid squares have a variety of development styles, ranging from conventional urban development and industrial parks to original rural and modern urban and suburban developments. Most grid squares have Local Centres, intended as local retail hubs and most with community facilities as well. Originally intended under the masterplan to sit alongside the Grid Roads, the Local Centres were mostly in fact built embedded in the communities.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">Roundabout</a> junctions were built at intersections because the grid roads were intended to carry large volumes of traffic: this type of junction is efficient at dealing with these volumes. Some major roads are <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">dual carriageway</a>, the others are <a href="/wiki/Single_carriageway" title="Single carriageway">single carriageway</a>. Along one side of each single carriageway grid road there is a (grassed) reservation to permit dualling or additional transport infrastructure at a later date. To date this has been limited. The edges of each grid square are landscaped and densely planted, some additionally have <a href="/wiki/Berm" title="Berm">berms</a>. Traffic movements are fast, with relatively little congestion since there are alternative routes to any particular destination other than during the (brief) peak periods. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_speed_limit" title="National speed limit">national speed limit</a> applies on the grid roads, although lower <a href="/wiki/Speed_limit" title="Speed limit">speed limits</a> have been introduced on some stretches to reduce accident rates. Pedestrians rarely need to cross grid roads <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/At-grade_intersection" title="At-grade intersection">at grade</a>, as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Underpass" title="Underpass">underpasses</a> and bridges exist in frequent places along each stretch of all of the grid roads. However, the new districts to be added by the <a href="/wiki/Expansion_plans_for_Milton_Keynes" title="Expansion plans for Milton Keynes">expansion plans for Milton Keynes</a> are departing from this model, with less separation and using 'at grade' crossings. This approach, which contradicts the original design ethos, has been a cause for conflict between residents and the Council who are often regarded as failing to preserve the unique development style of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Monitoring station data<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-localair_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-localair-30">[29]</a></sup> shows that pollution is lower than in other settlements of a similar size.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Redways:_a_network_of_shared_use_paths">The Redways: a network of shared use paths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Redways: a network of shared use paths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="625" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif/220px-Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif/330px-Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif/440px-Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Milton_Keynes_Redway.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cycleway network in Milton Keynes. The national cycle routes are highlighted in red. (Extracted from Openstreetmap.org<br/>
© OpenStreetMap contributors).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_redway_system" title="Milton Keynes redway system">Milton Keynes redway system</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" title="Segregated cycle facilities">Segregated cycle facilities</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shared_use_path" title="Shared use path">Shared use path</a></div>
<p>There is a separate network (approximately 125 miles or 200 kilometres total length) of <a href="/wiki/Shared_use_path" title="Shared use path">cycle and pedestrian routes</a>, the "<a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_redway_system" title="Milton Keynes redway system">redways</a>", that runs through the grid-squares and often runs alongside the grid-road network. This was designed to segregate slow moving cycle and pedestrian traffic from fast moving motor traffic. In practice, it is mainly used for leisure <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> rather than commuting, perhaps because the cycle routes are shared with pedestrians, cross the grid-roads via bridge or underpass rather than at grade, and because some take meandering scenic routes rather than straight lines. It is so called because it is generally surfaced with red tarmac. The national <a href="/wiki/Sustrans" title="Sustrans">Sustrans</a> national cycle network routes <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Route_6" title="National Cycle Route 6">6</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Route_51" title="National Cycle Route 51">51</a> take advantage of this system.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Height">Height</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Height">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2564" data-file-width="4005" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg/220px-The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg/330px-The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg/440px-The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Hub_Milton_Keynes_towers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Hub:MK, built between 2006 and 2008. The taller glass tower, Manhattan House, has fourteen stories.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The original design guidance declared that "no building [be] taller than the tallest tree". However, the <a href="/wiki/English_Partnerships#Milton_Keynes_Partnership" title="English Partnerships">Milton Keynes Partnership</a>, in its <a href="/wiki/Expansion_plans_for_Milton_Keynes" title="Expansion plans for Milton Keynes">expansion plans for Milton Keynes</a>, believed that <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">Central Milton Keynes</a> (and elsewhere) needed "landmark buildings" and subsequently lifted the height restriction for the area. As a result, high rise buildings have been built in the central business district. Four of the pedestrian underpasses were closed to 'normalise' the streetscape of Central Milton Keynes and the character of the area was set to change under government pressure to increase densities of development. These changes are being opposed by pressure groups such as <a href="/wiki/Urban_Eden" title="Urban Eden">Urban Eden</a> and the Milton Keynes Forum. More recent local plans have protected the existing boulevard framework and underpasses following the dissolution of Milton Keynes Partnership.</p>
<p>Recent large-scale buildings include <i>The Pinnacle:MK</i> on Midsummer Boulevard and the <i>Vizion</i> development on Avebury Boulevard. The Pinnacle was the largest office building to be constructed in Milton Keynes in 25 years. More recently the Network Rail National Centre has been built at the western limit of Silbury Boulevard; this building occupies a large land area but only rises to the equivalent of six storeys; a return towards the design of the original Central Milton Keynes developments.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linear_parks">Linear parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Linear parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caldecotte_Lake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="563" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Caldecotte_Lake.jpg/220px-Caldecotte_Lake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Caldecotte_Lake.jpg/330px-Caldecotte_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Caldecotte_Lake.jpg/440px-Caldecotte_Lake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caldecotte_Lake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Caldecotte Lake, Milton Keynes</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flood_plain" title="Flood plain">flood plains</a> of the <a href="/wiki/River_Great_Ouse" title="River Great Ouse">Great Ouse</a> and of its tributaries (the <a href="/wiki/River_Ouzel" title="River Ouzel">Ouzel</a> and some brooks) have been protected as <a href="/wiki/Linear_park" title="Linear park">linear parks</a> that run right through Milton Keynes. The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Canal" title="Grand Union Canal">Grand Union Canal</a> is another green route (and demonstrates the level geography of the area –  there is just one minor lock in its entire 10-mile (16 km) meandering route through from the southern boundary near <a href="/wiki/Fenny_Stratford" title="Fenny Stratford">Fenny Stratford</a> to the "Iron Trunk" <a href="/wiki/Navigable_aqueduct" title="Navigable aqueduct">Aqueduct</a> over the Ouse at <a href="/wiki/Wolverton" title="Wolverton">Wolverton</a> at its northern boundary). The <a href="/wiki/Park_system" title="Park system">Park system</a> was designed by <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architect" title="Landscape architect">landscape architect</a> Peter Youngman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> who also developed landscape precepts for all development areas: groups of grid squares were to be planted with different selections of trees and shrubs to give them distinct identities. However the landscaping of parks and of the grid roads was evolved under the leadership of Neil Higson,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> who from 1977 took over as Chief Landscape Architect and made the original grand but not entirely practical landscape plan more subtle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".22City_in_the_forest.22">"City in the forest"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title='Edit section: "City in the forest"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The original Development Corporation design concept aimed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker2_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-walker2-18">[17]</a></sup> for a "forest city" and its foresters planted millions of trees from its own nursery in Newlands in the following years. As of 2006, the urban area has 20 million trees. Following the <a href="/wiki/Liquidation" title="Liquidation">winding up</a> of the Development Corporation, the lavish landscapes of the Grid Roads and of the major parks were transferred to The <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Parks_Trust" title="Milton Keynes Parks Trust">Milton Keynes Parks Trust</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foundation_(charity)" title="Foundation (charity)">charity</a> which is independent from the municipal authority and which was intended to resist pressures to build on the parks over time. The Parks Trust is endowed with a portfolio of commercial properties, the income of which pay for the upkeep of the green spaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parkstrust1_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-parkstrust1-34">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_development_plans">Further development plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Further development plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%27City_Street%27,_Broughton_Gate,_Milton_Keynes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2938" data-file-width="4320" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/%27City_Street%27%2C_Broughton_Gate%2C_Milton_Keynes.jpg/220px-%27City_Street%27%2C_Broughton_Gate%2C_Milton_Keynes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/%27City_Street%27%2C_Broughton_Gate%2C_Milton_Keynes.jpg/330px-%27City_Street%27%2C_Broughton_Gate%2C_Milton_Keynes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/%27City_Street%27%2C_Broughton_Gate%2C_Milton_Keynes.jpg/440px-%27City_Street%27%2C_Broughton_Gate%2C_Milton_Keynes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%27City_Street%27,_Broughton_Gate,_Milton_Keynes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the new 'city streets', an extension of H7 Chaffron Way, in Broughton Gate.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Expansion_plans_for_Milton_Keynes" title="Expansion plans for Milton Keynes">Expansion plans for Milton Keynes</a></div>
<p>In January 2004, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister" title="Deputy Prime Minister">Deputy Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Prescott" title="John Prescott">John Prescott</a> announced<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian1_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-35">[34]</a></sup> the Government's plan to double the population of Milton Keynes by 2026. He appointed <a href="/wiki/English_Partnerships" title="English Partnerships">English Partnerships</a> (EP) to do so, taking planning controls away from Milton Keynes Borough Council and making EP the statutory planning authority. Their proposal for the next phase of expansion moves away from grid squares to large scale, mixed use, higher density development. The <a href="/wiki/Expansion_plans_for_Milton_Keynes" title="Expansion plans for Milton Keynes">more detailed article</a> expands on the details of their proposals. As the first stage in that plan, the Government expanded<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opsi1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-opsi1-36">[35]</a></sup> the boundaries of the designated area, adding large green-field expansion sites to the east and west that were to be developed by 2015.</p>
<p>In June 2004 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Partnership" title="Milton Keynes Partnership">Milton Keynes Partnership</a> Committee (MKPC), was created by the Government and was a committee of the Homes and Communities Agency (HCA), the national housing and regeneration agency for England. MKPC was created to ensure a co-ordinated approach to planning and delivery of growth and development in the ‘new city’. Milton Keynes Partnership was disbanded in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mkp1_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-mkp1-37">[36]</a></sup> holding its last meeting in March of that year. Its functions were folded back into the Homes and Communities Agency (HCA), with Milton Keynes Council handling planning permission for established areas of MK.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg/220px-MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg/330px-MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg/440px-MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MK_Bowl_Concert.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
65,000 capacity by the <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> <a href="/wiki/Bullet_in_a_Bible" title="Bullet in a Bible">Bullet in a Bible</a> concert at the <a href="/wiki/National_Bowl" title="National Bowl">National Bowl</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The open air <a href="/wiki/National_Bowl" title="National Bowl">National Bowl</a> is a 65,000 capacity venue for large scale events.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Wavendon" title="Wavendon">Wavendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Stables" title="The Stables">the Stables</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> provides a venue for <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a>, rock, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_classical_music" title="European classical music">classical</a>, pop and <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>. It is closely associated with jazz artists <a href="/wiki/Cleo_Laine" title="Cleo Laine">Cleo Laine</a> and the late <a href="/wiki/John_Dankworth" title="John Dankworth">John Dankworth</a>. The venue also hosts an annual <a href="/wiki/Summer_camp" title="Summer camp">summer camp</a> for young musicians.</p>
<p><a class="external text" href="https://www.facebook.com/Mk11Music" rel="nofollow">MK11 at Kiln Farm Club</a> is based within Kiln Farm Industrial Estate, off of Watling Street. In 2014 it was voted as <a class="external text" href="http://www.mkweb.co.uk/MK11-Kiln-Farm-Club-named-best-live-music-pub-Milton-Keynes-magazine/story-22250952-detail/story.html" rel="nofollow">MK's Best Live Music Venue</a> by readers of local culture magazine Monkey Kettle. That year also saw the venue face potential closure after it was served with a noise abatement order from the local council, following complaints from the neighbouring Sikh Temple. A petition was signed by 3,500 supporters to save the club; this, coupled with noise reduction measures implemented by the club's owners, meant that MK11 was able to stay open.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_literature">Arts and literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Arts and literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The municipal public art gallery, MK Gallery,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> presents free exhibitions of international contemporary art.</p>
<p>There are two museums:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a> complex which, as well as housing the museum of wartime cryptography, also hosts (separately) the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Computing" title="National Museum of Computing">National Museum of Computing</a> including a working replica of the <a href="/wiki/Colossus_computer" title="Colossus computer">Colossus computer</a>, and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Museum" title="Milton Keynes Museum">Milton Keynes Museum</a>, which includes the Stacey Hill Collection of rural life that existed before the foundation of MK and the original Concrete Cows.</li>
</ul>
<p>The 1,400 seat <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Theatre" title="Milton Keynes Theatre">Milton Keynes Theatre</a> opened in 1999. The theatre has an unusual feature: the ceiling can be lowered closing off the third tier (gallery) to create a more intimate space for smaller-scale productions. There are further performance spaces in Bletchley, Wolverton, <a href="/wiki/Woughton#Leadenhall" title="Woughton">Leadenhall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenley_Church_End" title="Shenley Church End">Shenley Church End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stantonbury" title="Stantonbury">Stantonbury</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walton_Hall_(Milton_Keynes)" title="Walton Hall (Milton Keynes)">Walton Hall</a>.</p>
<p>MK also has a literature scene, with groups like Speakeasy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> meeting regularly and hosting performance events, and former poetry and arts magazine, <a href="/wiki/Monkey_Kettle" title="Monkey Kettle">Monkey Kettle</a> which ran between 1999 and 2014. In addition, two <a href="/wiki/Performance_poetry" title="Performance poetry">performance poetry</a> groups exist  –  Poetry Kapow!,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> an offshoot of Monkey Kettle though now independent of the parent organisation, specialising in live, multi-discipline, interactive poetry/art/music events, usually featuring <a href="/wiki/Poetry_slam" title="Poetry slam">slams</a>; and Tongue in Chic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> a regular <a href="/wiki/Open_mic" title="Open mic">open mic</a> poetry event which features headline poets such as <a href="/wiki/John_Hegley" title="John Hegley">John Hegley</a>.</p>
<p>In May 2011 the outgoing Mayor, Debbie Brock, announced the appointment of Mark Niel as the first official Milton Keynes' Poet Laureate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Milton Keynes Arts Centre is situated in the historic village of <a href="/wiki/Great_Linford" title="Great Linford">Great Linford</a> in the north of MK, between Wolverton and Newport Pagnell. Milton Keynes Arts Centre offers a year round exhibitions, families workshops and courses. Situated across many of Great Linford Manor's exterior buildings (barns, <a href="/wiki/Almshouse" title="Almshouse">Almshouses</a>, Pavilions), the Arts Centre offers a special historical setting.</p>
<p>The Westbury Arts Centre is situated in the west of MK, near <a href="/wiki/Shenley_Church_End" title="Shenley Church End">Shenley Wood</a>. It is based in a 16th-century grade II listed Farmhouse building. The Art Centre has been providing spaces for professional working artists to create work since 1994. The oldest part of the house was built in the sixteenth century and has been greatly extended over the years. It has several acres of garden and is home to several protected species of bats and newts.</p>
<p>Milton Keynes also boasts several <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choirs</a> –  the Milton Keynes Chorale, the New English Singers, the Cornerstone Choir, Quorum,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> the Open University Choir, and others.</p>
<p>There is a variety of amateur drama groups, and amateur musical theatre groups.</p>
<p>Milton Keynes Forum is the registered <a href="/wiki/Civic_society" title="Civic society">civic society</a> for MK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_sculpture">Public sculpture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Public sculpture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ConcreteCows.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="629" data-file-width="1023" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/ConcreteCows.jpg/220px-ConcreteCows.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/ConcreteCows.jpg/330px-ConcreteCows.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/ConcreteCows.jpg/440px-ConcreteCows.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ConcreteCows.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Liz Leyh's iconic "<a href="/wiki/Concrete_Cows" title="Concrete Cows">Concrete Cows</a>"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Public sculpture in Milton Keynes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> includes work by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Jackson_(sculptor)" title="Philip Jackson (sculptor)">Philip Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Moreton" title="Nicolas Moreton">Nicolas Moreton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Rae" title="Ronald Rae">Ronald Rae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Frink" title="Elisabeth Frink">Elisabeth Frink</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a>'s headquarters are based in the Walton Hall district, though because this is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distance_learning" title="Distance learning">distance learning</a> institution, the only students resident on campus are approximately 200 full-time postgraduates. <a href="/wiki/Cranfield_University" title="Cranfield University">Cranfield University</a>, an all-postgraduate institution, is in nearby <a href="/wiki/Cranfield" title="Cranfield">Cranfield</a>, Bedfordshire. <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_College" title="Milton Keynes College">Milton Keynes College</a> provides <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> up to <a href="/wiki/Foundation_degree" title="Foundation degree">foundation degree</a> level, however a <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_Certificate_in_Education" title="Postgraduate Certificate in Education">Postgraduate Certificate in Education</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> course is available; run in partnership with and accredited by <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Brookes_University" title="Oxford Brookes University">Oxford Brookes University</a>.</p>
<p>In 1991 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leicester_Polytechnic" title="Leicester Polytechnic">Leicester Polytechnic</a> established a purpose-built <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_(United_Kingdom)" title="Polytechnic (United Kingdom)">polytechnic</a> campus in Kents Hill in Milton Keynes, opposite the Open University's Walton Hall site, which was officially opened by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> in 1992. This was originally branded 'The Polytechnic: Milton Keynes'. Later in 1992 Leicester Polytechnic gained <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> status and was renamed <a href="/wiki/De_Montfort_University" title="De Montfort University">De Montfort University</a>, and the site was rebranded 'De Montfort University Milton Keynes'. However, DMU closed the MK site in 2003 and the Open University has expanded to take over the buildings.</p>
<p>Although Milton Keynes does not yet have its own conventional local university, its founders hope that the <a href="/wiki/University_Campus_Milton_Keynes" title="University Campus Milton Keynes">University Campus Milton Keynes</a> will be the seed for a future 'Milton Keynes University'. MK is currently the UK's largest population centre without its own university proper.</p>
<p>Like most parts of the UK, the state secondary schools in Milton Keynes are <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_school" title="Comprehensive school">Comprehensive schools</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Stantonbury_Campus" title="Stantonbury Campus">Stantonbury Campus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denbigh_School" title="Denbigh School">Denbigh School</a>, although schools in the rest of Buckinghamshire still use the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tripartite_System" title="Tripartite System">Tripartite System</a>. Results are above the national average, though below that of the rest of Buckinghamshire –  but the <a href="/wiki/Demography" title="Demography">demography</a> of Milton Keynes is also far closer to the national average than is the latter. Access to selective schools is still possible in Milton Keynes as the grammar schools in Buckingham and Aylesbury accept some pupils from within the unitary authority area, with Buckinghamshire County Council operating bus services to ferry pupils to the schools.</p>
<p>Private schools in Milton Keynes include the 3-to-18 mixed sex <a href="/wiki/Webber_Independent_School" title="Webber Independent School">Webber Independent School</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> and the 2½-to-11 mixed sex Milton Keynes Preparatory School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Safety_Centre" title="Safety Centre">Safety Centre</a> is a purpose-built interactive centre which provides safety education to visiting schools and youth groups via its full-size interactive demonstrations known as Hazard Alley. Another educational organisation is the Milton Keynes City Discovery Centre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Bradwell_Abbey#Bradwell_Abbey_today" title="Bradwell Abbey">Bradwell Abbey</a>, which holds an extensive archive about Milton Keynes. MKCDC is therefore a research facility, as well as offering a broad education programme (with a focus on urban geography and local history) to schools, universities and professionals. MKCDC also holds an annual programme of events at the medieval <a href="/wiki/Priory" title="Priory">priory</a> site on which they are based.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_infrastructure">Government and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The responsible local government is <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Council" title="Milton Keynes Council">Milton Keynes Council</a>, which controls the <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Borough of Milton Keynes</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unitary_Authority" title="Unitary Authority">Unitary Authority</a>. About 90% of the population of the Borough lives in the urban area.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hospitals">Hospitals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hospitals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_University_Hospital" title="Milton Keynes University Hospital">Milton Keynes University Hospital</a>, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eaglestone,_Milton_Keynes" title="Eaglestone, Milton Keynes">Eaglestone</a> district, is an <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">NHS</a> <a href="/wiki/Hospital#General" title="Hospital">general hospital</a> with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accident_and_Emergency" title="Accident and Emergency">Accident and Emergency</a> unit. It is associated for <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">medical teaching purposes</a> with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Buckingham" title="University of Buckingham">University of Buckingham</a> medical school. The nearby <b>BMI Saxon Clinic</b> is a small private hospital.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_government_offices">UK government offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: UK government offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Legalisation Office of the UK <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> –  which issues <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apostille" title="Apostille">Apostille</a> certificates to prove that official documents are genuine –  is located in Milton Keynes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Government_Communications_Headquarters" title="Government Communications Headquarters">Government Communications Headquarters</a> (GCHQ) previously had been located in Milton Keynes (at <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a>), but moved to <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham" title="Cheltenham">Cheltenham</a> in the early 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications_and_media">Communications and media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Communications and media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Milton Keynes has two <a href="/wiki/Commercial_broadcasting" title="Commercial broadcasting">commercial radio</a> stations, <a href="/wiki/Heart_Four_Counties" title="Heart Four Counties">Heart Four Counties</a> covering Buckinghamshire, Bedfordshire, Hertfordshire and Northamptonshire, and <a href="/wiki/MKFM" title="MKFM">MKFM</a>.</p>
<p>The first commercial radio station for Milton Keynes was established in 1989 under the name <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horizon_Radio_(UK)" title="Horizon Radio (UK)">Horizon Radio</a>. It was subsequently renamed Heart MK in 2009 after being bought out by <a href="/wiki/Global_Radio" title="Global Radio">Global Radio</a>. Heart MK was merged with <a href="/wiki/Heart_Northants" title="Heart Northants">Heart Northants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_Dunstable" title="Heart Dunstable">Heart Dunstable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heart_Bedford" title="Heart Bedford">Heart Bedford</a> in 2010 to form <a href="/wiki/Heart_Four_Counties" title="Heart Four Counties">Heart Four Counties</a>.</p>
<p><a class="external text" href="http://www.mkfm.com" rel="nofollow">MKFM</a> launched in 2011, initially broadcasting on internet, later on DAB Digital Radio full-time and also on twice-yearly 28-day FM trial, <a href="/wiki/Restricted_Service_Licence" title="Restricted Service Licence">Restricted Service Licence</a>. In December 2014, it applied for a full-time, permanent licence through Ofcom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> On 19 March 2015, Ofcom granted this full-time FM licence to MKFM. Transmissions were switched from the Pod at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadium_MK" title="Stadium MK">Stadium MK</a> to the station's new studio on Monday 17 August 2015 at <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes_Shopping_Centre" title="Central Milton Keynes Shopping Centre">intu Milton Keynes</a> and the station launched on 106.3FM at 6am on Monday 7 September 2015.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Three_Counties_Radio" title="BBC Three Counties Radio">BBC Three Counties Radio</a> is the local <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">BBC Radio</a> station, covering Buckinghamshire, Bedfordshire and Hertfordshire, but has different programming from the <a href="/wiki/Bow_Brickhill" title="Bow Brickhill">Bow Brickhill</a> transmitter at breakfast. CRMK Online<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> is a voluntary station broadcasting on the Internet.</p>
<p>For television, the area is in the overlap between the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_transmitting_station" title="Oxford transmitting station">Oxford</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Heath_transmitting_station" title="Sandy Heath transmitting station">Sandy</a> transmitters and so receives <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_South_Today#Oxford_opt-out" title="BBC South Today">BBC South</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Look_East" title="BBC Look East">BBC East</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> <a href="/wiki/ITV_News_Meridian" title="ITV News Meridian">Meridian</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_News_Anglia" title="ITV News Anglia">Anglia</a>.</p>
<p>As of October 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Milton Keynes has one free-to-residents local newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Citizen" title="Milton Keynes Citizen">Milton Keynes Citizen</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Milton Keynes has consistently benefited from above-average economic growth. Outside of London it is ranked as one of the most attractive places for business along with Oxford, Cambridge and Manchester.</p>
<p>In November 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Citizen" title="Milton Keynes Citizen">Milton Keynes Citizen</a> reported ratings company <a href="/wiki/Experian" title="Experian">Experian</a> as describing Milton Keynes as one of the leaders in a prospective economic recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizen181012_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-citizen181012-55">[54]</a></sup> The same report quoted the Estate Gazette as placing it first outside the M25 for office property growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizen181012_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-citizen181012-55">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Milton Keynes is home to several national and international companies, including the UK headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Home_Retail_Group" title="Home Retail Group">Argos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domino%27s_Pizza" title="Domino's Pizza">Domino's Pizza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification" title="Marshall Amplification">Marshall Amplification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suzuki" title="Suzuki">Suzuki</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_AG" title="Volkswagen AG">Volkswagen AG</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yamaha" title="Yamaha">Yamaha Kemble</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015, it was announced that Milton Keynes had seen the highest growth in jobs out of the biggest 64 towns and cities in the UK during the preceding decade. Milton Keynes saw its number of jobs increase by 18.2 per cent between 2004 and 2013, followed by London on 17.1 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Milton_Keynes" title="Sport in Milton Keynes">Sport in Milton Keynes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG/220px-Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG/330px-Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG/440px-Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denbigh_stadium_east_stand_16_May_07.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stadium MK (in 2007)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Milton Keynes has professional teams in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_Football" title="Association Football">football</a> (<a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons_F.C." title="Milton Keynes Dons F.C.">Milton Keynes Dons F.C.</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadium:mk" title="Stadium:mk">Stadium:mk</a>), in <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> (<a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Lightning" title="Milton Keynes Lightning">Milton Keynes Lightning</a>), and in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> (<a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a>).</p>
<p>Milton Keynes is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Xscape_(building)" title="Xscape (building)">Xscape</a> indoor ski slope, the Airkix indoor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sky_diving" title="Sky diving">sky diving</a> facility, the Formula Fast Indoor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karting" title="Karting">Karting</a> centre, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Badminton_Centre" title="National Badminton Centre">National Badminton Centre</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Centre">Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">Central Milton Keynes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Shopping_Centre" title="Milton Keynes Shopping Centre">Milton Keynes Shopping Centre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">Milton Keynes Central railway station</a></div>
<p>As a key element of the New Town vision, Milton Keynes has a purpose built centre, with a very large "covered high street" shopping centre, theatre, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_gallery" title="Art gallery">art gallery</a>, two multiplex cinemas, hotels, business district, ecumenical church, <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Borough Council offices</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">central railway station</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_amenities">Other amenities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other amenities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gnarled_Tree.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1829" data-file-width="2081" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gnarled_Tree.jpg/220px-Gnarled_Tree.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gnarled_Tree.jpg/330px-Gnarled_Tree.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gnarled_Tree.jpg/440px-Gnarled_Tree.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gnarled_Tree.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Part of the Blue Lagoon</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Near the central station, the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_central_bus_station" title="Milton Keynes central bus station">Milton Keynes central bus station</a> has become a youth club called 'the Buszy' with a purpose-built covered "urban <a href="/wiki/Skateboard" title="Skateboard">skateboarding</a>" arena, but the wide expanses and slopes of the station plaza remain very popular among skaters.</li>
<li>There is a high security prison, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodhill_(HM_Prison)" title="Woodhill (HM Prison)">HMP Woodhill</a>, on the western boundary.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willen_Lake" title="Willen Lake">Willen Lakeside Park</a> hosts <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watersports" title="Watersports">watersports</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willen_Lake" title="Willen Lake">North Lake</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bird_sanctuary" title="Bird sanctuary">bird sanctuary</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Blue_Lagoon_Local_Nature_Reserve" title="Blue Lagoon Local Nature Reserve">Blue Lagoon Local Nature Reserve</a> is in Bletchley.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_towns_and_villages">Original towns and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Original towns and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bletchley_Park.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1101" data-file-width="2041" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bletchley_Park.jpg/220px-Bletchley_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bletchley_Park.jpg/330px-Bletchley_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bletchley_Park.jpg/440px-Bletchley_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bletchley_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
During the Second World War, British, Polish and American cryptographers at <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a> broke a large number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis</a> codes and ciphers, including the German <a href="/wiki/Enigma_machine" title="Enigma machine">Enigma machine</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bradwell-windmill.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bradwell-windmill.JPG/220px-Bradwell-windmill.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bradwell-windmill.JPG/330px-Bradwell-windmill.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bradwell-windmill.JPG/440px-Bradwell-windmill.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg/220px-StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg/330px-StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg/440px-StonyStratford_HighStreet01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG/220px-MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG/330px-MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG/440px-MiltonKeynesPeacePagoda01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
