<a href="/wiki/Peace_Pagoda" title="Peace Pagoda">Peace Pagoda</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Milton Keynes consists of many pre-existing towns and villages, as well as new infill developments. The designated area outside the four main towns (Bletchley, Newport Pagnell, Stony Stratford, Wolverton) was largely rural farmland but included many picturesque North Buckinghamshire villages and hamlets: <a href="/wiki/Bradwell,_Milton_Keynes" title="Bradwell, Milton Keynes">Bradwell</a> village and <a href="/wiki/Bradwell_Abbey" title="Bradwell Abbey">its Abbey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Broughton, Milton Keynes">Broughton</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caldecotte,_Milton_Keynes" title="Caldecotte, Milton Keynes">Caldecotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fenny_Stratford" title="Fenny Stratford">Fenny Stratford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Linford" title="Great Linford">Great Linford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loughton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Loughton, Milton Keynes">Loughton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Middleton, Milton Keynes">Milton Keynes Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Bradwell" title="New Bradwell">New Bradwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenley_Brook_End" title="Shenley Brook End">Shenley Brook End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenley_Church_End" title="Shenley Church End">Shenley Church End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simpson,_Milton_Keynes" title="Simpson, Milton Keynes">Simpson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stantonbury" title="Stantonbury">Stantonbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tattenhoe" title="Tattenhoe">Tattenhoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tongwell" title="Tongwell">Tongwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Walton, Milton Keynes">Walton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_Eaton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Water Eaton, Milton Keynes">Water Eaton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wavendon" title="Wavendon">Wavendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willen" title="Willen">Willen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woolstone,_Milton_Keynes" title="Woolstone, Milton Keynes">Great and Little Woolstone</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woughton_on_the_Green" title="Woughton on the Green">Woughton on the Green</a>. The historical settlements have been focal points for the modern development of the new town. Every grid square has historical antecedents, if only in the field names. The more obvious ones are listed below and most have more detailed articles.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bletchley" title="Bletchley">Bletchley</a> was first recorded in the 12th century as <i>Blechelai</i>. <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_railway_station" title="Bletchley railway station">Its station</a> was a major <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> junction (the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Western_Railway" title="London and North Western Railway">London and North Western Railway</a> with the Oxford-Cambridge <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Line" title="Varsity Line">Varsity Line</a>), leading to the substantial urban growth in the town in that period. It expanded to absorb the villages of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_Eaton_(Milton_Keynes)" title="Water Eaton (Milton Keynes)">Water Eaton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fenny_Stratford" title="Fenny Stratford">Fenny Stratford</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a> was home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_Code_and_Cypher_School" title="Government Code and Cypher School">Government Code and Cypher School</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enigma_code" title="Enigma code">Enigma code</a> was cracked here, and the building housed what was arguably the world's first programmable computer, <a href="/wiki/History_of_computing_hardware" title="History of computing hardware">Colossus</a>. The house is now a museum of war memorabilia, cryptography and computing.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictine" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> <a href="/wiki/Priory" title="Priory">Priory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bradwell_Abbey" title="Bradwell Abbey">Bradwell Abbey</a> at <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradwell_(Milton_Keynes)" title="Bradwell (Milton Keynes)">Bradwell</a></b> was of major economic importance in this area of north Buckinghamshire before the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a>. The routes of the medieval trackways (many of which are now Redways or bridleways) converge on the site from some distance. Nowadays there is only a small medieval chapel and a manor house occupying the site.</p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/New_Bradwell" title="New Bradwell">New Bradwell</a></b>, to the north of the medieval Bradwell (Abbey) and just across the canal and the railway to the east of Wolverton, was built specifically for railway workers. It has a working <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmill</a>, although technically this lies just a few yards outside of the parish boundary. The level bed of the old <a href="/wiki/Wolverton_to_Newport_Pagnell_Line" title="Wolverton to Newport Pagnell Line">Wolverton to Newport Pagnell Line</a> ends here and has been converted to a Redway, making it a favourite route for cycling.</p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Great_Linford" title="Great Linford">Great Linford</a></b> appears in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a> as <i>Linforde</i>, and features a church dedicated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew" title="Saint Andrew">Saint Andrew</a>, dating from 1215. Today, the outer buildings of the 17th century <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">manor house</a> form an <a href="/wiki/Arts_centre" title="Arts centre">arts centre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Linford_Manor" title="Linford Manor">Linford Manor</a> is a prestigious recording studio.</p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Middleton, Milton Keynes">Milton Keynes Village</a></b> is the original village to which the New Town owes its name. The original village is still evident, with a pleasant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thatch" title="Thatch">thatched</a> <a href="/wiki/Pub" title="Pub">pub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Village_hall" title="Village hall">village hall</a>, church and traditional housing. The area around the village has reverted to its original name of <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middleton_(Milton_Keynes_Village)" title="Middleton (Milton Keynes Village)">Middleton</a></b>, as shown on old maps of the 1700s. The oldest<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pastpresentfuture_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-pastpresentfuture-58">[57]</a></sup> surviving domestic building in the area, a 14th-century manor house, is here.</p>
<p>There has been a market in <b><a href="/wiki/Stony_Stratford" title="Stony Stratford">Stony Stratford</a></b> since 1194 (by charter of <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">King Richard I</a>). The <i>Rose and Crown Inn</i> at Stratford is reputedly the last place the <a href="/wiki/Princes_in_the_Tower" title="Princes in the Tower">Princes in the Tower</a> were seen alive.</p>
<p>The manor house of <b><a href="/wiki/Walton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Walton, Milton Keynes">Walton</a></b> village, <b><a href="/wiki/Walton_Hall,_Milton_Keynes" title="Walton Hall, Milton Keynes">Walton Hall</a></b>, is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a> and the tiny <a href="/wiki/Parish_church" title="Parish church">parish church</a> (deconsecrated) is in its grounds.</p>
<p>The tiny Parish Church (1680) at <a href="/wiki/Willen" title="Willen">Willen</a> contains the only unaltered building by the architect and physicist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">Robert Hooke</a>. Nearby, there is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> Temple and a <a href="/wiki/Peace_Pagoda" title="Peace Pagoda">Peace Pagoda</a> which was built in 1980 and was the first in the western world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> The district borders the <a href="/wiki/River_Ouzel" title="River Ouzel">River Ouzel</a>: there is a large <a href="/wiki/Balancing_lake" title="Balancing lake">balancing lake</a> here, to capture <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">flash floods</a> before they cause problems downstream on the <a href="/wiki/River_Great_Ouse" title="River Great Ouse">River Great Ouse</a>. The north basin is a wildlife sanctuary and a favourite of migrating aquatic birds. The south basin is for leisure use, favoured by wind surfers and dinghy sailors. The circuit of the lakes is a favoured "fun run".</p>
<p>The original <a href="/wiki/Wolverton" title="Wolverton">Wolverton</a> was a medieval settlement just north and west of today's town. The <a href="/wiki/Ridge_and_furrow" title="Ridge and furrow">ridge and furrow</a> pattern of agriculture can still be seen in the nearby fields and the Saxon (rebuilt in 1819) <b>Church of the Holy Trinity</b> still stands next to the Norman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motte_and_Bailey" title="Motte and Bailey">Motte and Bailey</a> site. Modern Wolverton was a 19th-century New Town built to house the workers at the <a href="/wiki/Wolverton_railway_works" title="Wolverton railway works">Wolverton railway works</a>, which built engines and carriages for the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Western_Railway" title="London and North Western Railway">London and North Western Railway</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy.2C_demography.2C_geography_and_politics">Economy, demography, geography and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy, demography, geography and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Borough of Milton Keynes</a></div>
<p>Data on the economy, demography and politics of Milton Keynes are collected at the Borough level and are detailed at <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes#Economy" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Economy of the Borough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes#Demographics" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Demographics of the Borough</a>. However, since the urban area is predominant in the Borough, it is reasonable to assume that, other than for agriculture, the figures are broadly the same.</p>
<p>Milton Keynes is one of the more successful (per capita) economies in the South East, with a <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">gross value added</a> per capita index that was 47% higher than the national average (2005 data).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Average wages place it in the top five nationally (2015 data).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>With 99.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_and_Medium_Enterprise" title="Small and Medium Enterprise">SMEs</a>, just 0.6% of businesses locally employ more than 250 people:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKLEAR_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-MKLEAR-62">[61]</a></sup> the more notable of these include the <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander_UK" title="Santander UK">Santander UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercedes_Benz" title="Mercedes Benz">Mercedes Benz</a>. Of the remaining enterprises, 81.5% employ fewer than 10 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKLEAR_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-MKLEAR-62">[61]</a></sup> The 'professional, scientific and technical sector' contributes the largest number of business units, 16.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKLEAR_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-MKLEAR-62">[61]</a></sup> The retail sector is the largest contributor of employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKLEAR_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-MKLEAR-62">[61]</a></sup> Milton Keynes has one of the highest business start-ups in England and the start-up levels remained high during the 2009/10 recession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKLEAR_62-4"><a href="#cite_note-MKLEAR-62">[61]</a></sup> Although Education, Health and Public Administration are important contributors to employment, the contribution is significantly less than in England or the South East as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKLEAR_62-5"><a href="#cite_note-MKLEAR-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The population is significantly younger than the national averages: 22.6% of the Borough population are aged under 16 compared with 19.0% in England; 12.1% are aged 65+ compared with 17.3% in England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> According to 2011 census, the ethnic group categories makeup of Milton Keynes Urban Area is: 78.4% <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a>, 8.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Asian_People" title="South Asian People">South Asian</a>, 7.5% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_People" title="Black People">Black</a>, 3.5% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_Race" title="Mixed Race">Mixed Race</a>, 1.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_British" title="Chinese British">Chinese</a> and other Asian, and 0.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Other_ethnic_group_(United_Kingdom_Census)" title="Other ethnic group (United Kingdom Census)">other ethnic group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_parishes.2C_community_councils_and_districts">Modern parishes, community councils and districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Modern parishes, community councils and districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Borough of Milton Keynes is fully <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" title="Civil parishes in England">parished</a>. These are the parishes, community councils and the districts they contain, within Milton Keynes itself. For a list of parishes in the Borough, see <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Milton_Keynes#Rest_of_the_borough" title="Borough of Milton Keynes">Borough of Milton Keynes (Rest of the borough)</a></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bletchley_and_Fenny_Stratford" title="Bletchley and Fenny Stratford">Bletchley and Fenny Stratford</a>: Brick fields, Central <a href="/wiki/Bletchley" title="Bletchley">Bletchley</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denbigh_North" title="Denbigh North">Denbigh North</a>, Denbigh East, Denbigh West, Fenny Lock, <a href="/wiki/Fenny_Stratford" title="Fenny Stratford">Fenny Stratford</a>, Granby, Mount Farm, <a href="/wiki/Newton_Leys" title="Newton Leys">Newton Leys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_Eaton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Water Eaton, Milton Keynes">Water Eaton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bradwell,_Milton_Keynes" title="Bradwell, Milton Keynes">Bradwell</a>: Bradwell, Bradwell Common, Bradwell village, Heelands, Rooksley</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bradwell_Abbey" title="Bradwell Abbey">Bradwell Abbey</a>: Bradwell Abbey, Kiln Farm, Stacey Bushes, <a href="/wiki/Two_Mile_Ash" title="Two Mile Ash">Two Mile Ash</a>, Wymbush</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Broughton, Milton Keynes">Broughton</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_(civil_parish)" title="Milton Keynes (civil parish)">Milton Keynes</a> (shared parish council): Atterbury, Brook Furlong, <a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Broughton, Milton Keynes">Broughton</a>, Fox Milne, <a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Middleton, Milton Keynes">Middleton</a> (including Milton Keynes Village), Northfield, Oakgrove, Pineham</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Campbell_Park" title="Campbell Park">Campbell Park</a>: Fishermead, Newlands, Oldbrook, Springfield, <a href="/wiki/Willen" title="Willen">Willen and Willen Lake</a>, Winterhill, <a href="/wiki/Woolstone,_Milton_Keynes" title="Woolstone, Milton Keynes">Woolstone</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">Central Milton Keynes</a>: Central Milton Keynes and Campbell Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Linford" title="Great Linford">Great Linford</a>: Blakelands, Bolbeck Park, Conniburrow, Downs Barn, Downhead Park, Great Linford, Giffard Park, Neath Hill, Pennyland, Tongwell, Willen Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kents_Hill,_Monkston_and_Brinklow" title="Kents Hill, Monkston and Brinklow">Kents Hill, Monkston and Brinklow</a>: Brinklow, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kents_Hill,_Milton_Keynes" title="Kents Hill, Milton Keynes">Kents Hill</a>, Kingston, Monkston</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Loughton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Loughton, Milton Keynes">Loughton</a>: Loughton, Loughton Lodge, Great Holm, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knowlhill" title="Knowlhill">Knowlhill</a> (including <a href="/wiki/National_Bowl" title="National Bowl">the Bowl</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Bradwell" title="New Bradwell">New Bradwell</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Woughton" title="Old Woughton">Old Woughton</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woughton_on_the_Green" title="Woughton on the Green">Woughton on the Green</a>, Woughton Park, Passmore (formerly Tinkers Bridge North).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shenley_Brook_End" title="Shenley Brook End">Shenley Brook End</a>: Emerson Valley, Furzton, Kingsmead, Shenley Brook End, Snelshall, <a href="/wiki/Tattenhoe" title="Tattenhoe">Tattenhoe</a>, Tattenhoe Park, <a href="/wiki/Westcroft" title="Westcroft">Westcroft</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shenley_Church_End" title="Shenley Church End">Shenley Church End</a>: Crownhill, Grange Farm, Hazeley, Medbourne, Oakhill, Oxley Park, Shenley Church End, Woodhill</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simpson,_Milton_Keynes" title="Simpson, Milton Keynes">Simpson</a>: Ashland, Simpson, West Ashland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stantonbury" title="Stantonbury">Stantonbury</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bancroft,_Milton_Keynes" title="Bancroft, Milton Keynes">Bancroft/Bancroft Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stantonbury#Blue_Bridge" title="Stantonbury">Blue Bridge</a>, Bradville, Linford Wood, Oakridge Park, Stantonbury, Stantonbury Fields</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stony_Stratford" title="Stony Stratford">Stony Stratford</a>: Fullers Slade, Galley Hill, Stony Stratford</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walton,_Milton_Keynes" title="Walton, Milton Keynes">Walton</a>: Brown's Wood, Caldecotte, Old Farm Park, Tilbrook, Tower Gate, Walnut Tree, Walton, <a href="/wiki/Walton_Hall,_Milton_Keynes" title="Walton Hall, Milton Keynes">Walton Hall</a>, Walton Park, Wavendon Gate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Bletchley" title="West Bletchley">West Bletchley</a>: Far Bletchley, Old Bletchley, West Bletchley, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denbigh_Hall" title="Denbigh Hall">Denbigh Hall</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wolverton_and_Greenleys" title="Wolverton and Greenleys">Wolverton and Greenleys</a>: Greenleys, Hodge Lea, Stonebridge, <a href="/wiki/Wolverton" title="Wolverton">Wolverton</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Wolverton" title="Old Wolverton">Old Wolverton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Woughton" title="Woughton">Woughton</a>: Beanhill, Bleak Hall, Coffee Hall, Eaglestone, <a href="/wiki/National_Bowl#Elfield_Park" title="National Bowl">Elfield Park</a>, Leadenhall, Netherfield, Peartree Bridge, Redmoor, Tinkers Bridge.</li>
</ul>

<td style="width:33%"><img alt="" data-file-height="17" data-file-width="17" height="17" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/South.svg/17px-South.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/South.svg/26px-South.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/South.svg/34px-South.svg.png 2x" title="South" width="17"/></td>

<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Bicester" title="Bicester">Bicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a></td>
<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Leighton_Buzzard" title="Leighton Buzzard">Leighton Buzzard</a> or <a href="/wiki/Winslow,_Buckinghamshire" title="Winslow, Buckinghamshire">Winslow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury" title="Aylesbury">Aylesbury</a></td>
<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Toddington,_Bedfordshire" title="Toddington, Bedfordshire">Toddington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dunstable" title="Dunstable">Dunstable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a></td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ed_Slater" title="Ed Slater">Ed Slater</a>, professional rugby player for <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Tigers" title="Leicester Tigers">Leicester Tigers</a> who went to Two Mile Ash School and Denbigh Secondary School.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dele_Alli" title="Dele Alli">Dele Alli</a>, professional footballer for <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hostpur</a> who started his career with <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons_F.C." title="Milton Keynes Dons F.C.">Milton Keynes Dons</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_B-Lynch" title="Christopher B-Lynch">Christopher B-Lynch</a>, (visiting) Professor of Obstetrics and Gynaecology at <a href="/wiki/Cranfield_University" title="Cranfield University">Cranfield University</a>, responsible for inventing the eponymously named <a href="/wiki/B-Lynch_suture" title="B-Lynch suture">B-Lynch suture</a> which is used to treat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-partum_haemorrhage" title="Post-partum haemorrhage">post-partum haemorrhage</a> due to <a href="/wiki/Uterine_atony" title="Uterine atony">uterine atony</a> worked at Milton Keynes General Hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Baggaley" title="Andrew Baggaley">Andrew Baggaley</a>, English table tennis champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sam_Baldock" title="Sam Baldock">Sam Baldock</a>, professional footballer for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_Albion" title="Brighton and Hove Albion">Brighton and Hove Albion</a>, who began his football career at MK Dons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Errol_Barnett" title="Errol Barnett">Errol Barnett</a>, an anchor and correspondent for <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> is from Milton Keynes. He lived in Crownhill and attended Holmwood First School and Two Mile Ash <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">Middle School</a> before moving to the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emily_Bergl" title="Emily Bergl">Emily Bergl</a>, an actress famous for her roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Desperate_Housewives" title="Desperate Housewives">Desperate Housewives</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shameless_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Shameless (U.S. TV series)">Shameless</a></i>. Bergl was born in Milton Keynes, to an Irish mother and an English architect father.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_Clarke_(athlete)" title="Christopher Clarke (athlete)">Chris Clarke</a>, English sprinter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adam_Ficek" title="Adam Ficek">Adam Ficek</a>, drummer of London band <a href="/wiki/Babyshambles" title="Babyshambles">Babyshambles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lee_Hasdell" title="Lee Hasdell">Lee Hasdell</a>, professional Mixed martial artist and Kickboxer, and pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">Mixed martial arts</a> in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfighter_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-totalfighter-74">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Hildreth" title="James Hildreth">James Hildreth</a>, cricketer who plays for <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> and has played for England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shaun_Hutson" title="Shaun Hutson">Shaun Hutson</a>, Novelist of horror novels and dark urban thrillers, has lived in Milton Keynes for several years.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liam_Kelly_(footballer_born_1990)" title="Liam Kelly (footballer born 1990)">Liam Kelly</a>, professional footballer for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic" title="Oldham Athletic">Oldham Athletic</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Marshall_(businessman)" title="Jim Marshall (businessman)">Jim Marshall</a> (1923-2012), founder and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification" title="Marshall Amplification">Marshall Amplification</a> was living in and ran his business from Milton Keynes when he died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gordon_Moakes" title="Gordon Moakes">Gordon Moakes</a>, the bassist for the London-based rock band <a href="/wiki/Bloc_Party" title="Bloc Party">Bloc Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clare_Nasir" title="Clare Nasir">Clare Nasir</a>, the meteorologist, TV and radio personality, was born in Milton Keynes in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Craig_Pickering" title="Craig Pickering">Craig Pickering</a>, English sprinter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarah_Pinborough" title="Sarah Pinborough">Sarah Pinborough</a>, English horror writer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ian_Poulter" title="Ian Poulter">Ian Poulter</a>, PGA &amp; European Tour golf professional. Member of the 2010 and 2012 European Ryder Cup Teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Randall_(footballer)" title="Mark Randall (footballer)">Mark Randall</a>, professional footballer for <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons_F.C." title="Milton Keynes Dons F.C.">Milton Keynes Dons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eddie_Richards" title="Eddie Richards">Eddie Richards</a>, Britain's godfather of house music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greg_Rutherford" title="Greg Rutherford">Greg Rutherford</a>, long jump gold medallist for <a href="/wiki/Team_GB" title="Team GB">Team GB</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Olympic_Games" title="2012 Olympic Games">2012 Olympic Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jack_Trevor_Story" title="Jack Trevor Story">Jack Trevor Story</a>, novelist, was a long-term resident of Milton Keynes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sam_Tomkins" title="Sam Tomkins">Sam Tomkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan Warriors</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a> international <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> player, was born in Milton Keynes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a> (1912-1954), played a significant role in the creation of the modern computer. He lodged at the Crown Inn, <a href="/wiki/Shenley_Brook_End" title="Shenley Brook End">Shenley Brook End</a>, while working at <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kevin_Whately" title="Kevin Whately">Kevin Whately</a> lives in <a href="/wiki/Woburn_Sands" title="Woburn Sands">Woburn Sands</a>, in the Milton Keynes urban area.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dan_Wheldon" title="Dan Wheldon">Dan Wheldon</a> (1978-2011), Indy car driver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Williams_(footballer_born_1995)" title="George Williams (footballer born 1995)">George Williams</a>, professional footballer for <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pete_Winkelman" title="Pete Winkelman">Pete Winkelman</a>, Chairman of <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons_F.C." title="Milton Keynes Dons F.C.">Milton Keynes Dons</a> Football Club, owner of <a href="/wiki/Great_Linford#Linford_Manor" title="Great Linford">Linford Manor</a> recording studios, long term resident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bands">Bands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capdown" title="Capdown">Capdown</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ska_punk" title="Ska punk">ska punk</a> band, came from and formed in Milton Keynes in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fellsilent" title="Fellsilent">Fellsilent</a>, the metal band, come from and formed in Milton Keynes in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tesseract_(band)" title="Tesseract (band)">Tesseract</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Djent" title="Djent">djent</a> band formed as a full live act in Milton Keynes in 2007. Tesseract's guitarist, songwriter and producer Acle Kahney is also a former member of Fellsilent.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hacktivist_(band)" title="Hacktivist (band)">Hacktivist</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grime_(music)" title="Grime (music)">Grime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djent" title="Djent">djent</a> band formed in 2011.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RavenEye" title="RavenEye">RavenEye</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band, formed in Milton Keynes in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span id="Magna_Park.2C_Milton_Keynes"></span></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG/220px-BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG/330px-BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG/440px-BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BradwellAqueduct-GUC.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Canal" title="Grand Union Canal">Grand Union Canal</a> passes over Grafton Street at Bradwell via the modern Bradwell Aqueduct</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Buses_in_Milton_Keynes" title="Buses in Milton Keynes">Buses in Milton Keynes</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Canal" title="Grand Union Canal">Grand Union Canal</a> between London and Birmingham provides a major axis in the design of Milton Keynes.</p>
<p>Milton Keynes has five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_stations" title="Railway stations">railway stations</a>. <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">Milton Keynes Central</a> is served by inter-city services. <a href="/wiki/Wolverton_railway_station" title="Wolverton railway station">Wolverton</a>, Milton Keynes Central and <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_railway_station" title="Bletchley railway station">Bletchley</a> stations are on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fenny_Stratford_railway_station" title="Fenny Stratford railway station">Fenny Stratford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bow_Brickhill_railway_station" title="Bow Brickhill railway station">Bow Brickhill</a> are on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marston_Vale_Line" title="Marston Vale Line">Marston Vale Line</a>. <a href="/wiki/Woburn_Sands_railway_station" title="Woburn Sands railway station">Woburn Sands railway station</a>, also on the Marston Vale line, is in the small town of <a href="/wiki/Woburn_Sands" title="Woburn Sands">Woburn Sands</a> just inside the urban area.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a> runs along the east flank of MK and serves it from junctions 13, 14, and 15A. The <a href="/wiki/A5_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A5 road (Great Britain)">A5 road</a> runs right through MK as a <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade separated</a> <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">dual carriageway</a>. Other main roads are the <a href="/wiki/A509_road" title="A509 road">A509</a>, linking Milton Keynes with Wellingborough and Kettering, and the <a href="/wiki/A421_road" title="A421 road">A421</a> and <a href="/wiki/A422_road" title="A422 road">A422</a>, both running west towards <a href="/wiki/Buckingham" title="Buckingham">Buckingham</a> and east towards <a href="/wiki/Bedford" title="Bedford">Bedford</a>. Proximity to the M1 has led to construction of a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distribution_centre" title="Distribution centre">distribution centres</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Magna_Park,_Milton_Keynes" title="Magna Park, Milton Keynes">Magna Park</a> at the A421/A5130 junction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many long-distance coaches stop at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_coachway" title="Milton Keynes coachway">Milton Keynes coachway</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> (beside M1 Junction 14), some 3.3 miles (5.3 km) from the centre (or 4 mi or 6.4 km from Milton Keynes Central railway station).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> There is also a <a href="/wiki/Park_and_ride" title="Park and ride">park and ride</a> car park on the site. Regional coaches stop at Milton Keynes Central.</p>
<p>The main bus operator is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arriva_Milton_Keynes" title="Arriva Milton Keynes">Arriva Milton Keynes</a>, providing a number of routes which mainly pass through or serve <a href="/wiki/Central_Milton_Keynes" title="Central Milton Keynes">Central Milton Keynes</a>. Milton Keynes is also served by Arriva-branded services from <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury" title="Aylesbury">Aylesbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a> as well and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_East" title="Stagecoach East">Stagecoach East</a> which operate routes to <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Midlands" title="Stagecoach Midlands">Stagecoach Midlands</a> which operates routes to <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>. Some local services are run by independent operators such as Z&amp;S International and Centrebus.</p>
<p>Milton Keynes is served by (and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_redway_system#National_Cycle_Network" title="Milton Keynes redway system">provides part of</a>) routes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCR_6" title="NCR 6">6</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCR_51" title="NCR 51">51</a> on the <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Network" title="National Cycle Network">National Cycle Network</a>.</p>
<p>The nearest <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a>, accessible by Stagecoach route 99 from MK Central station, which runs with wheelchair-accessible coaches. There is a direct rail connection to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_International_railway_station" title="Birmingham International railway station">Birmingham International</a> station for <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">Birmingham Airport</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Cranfield_Airport" title="Cranfield Airport">Cranfield Airport</a>, an airfield, is 6 miles (10 km) from the centre. (Although Milton Keynes is allocated an <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">International Air Transport Association airport code</a> of <b>KYN</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> it does not have an airport. Proposals in 1971 for a third London airport at (relatively) nearby <a href="/wiki/Cublington" title="Cublington">Cublington</a> were rejected).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns">Twin towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Twin towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg"><img alt="Flag of the Netherlands.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/20px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Almere" title="Almere">Almere</a>, Netherlands<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Milton Keynes experiences an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Cfb</i>) similar to almost all of the United Kingdom. Recorded temperature extremes range from 34.6 °C (94.3 °F)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> during July 2006, to as low as −20.6 °C (−5.1 °F)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> on 25 February 1947. More recently the temperature fell to −16.3 °C (2.7 °F)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> on 20 December 2010</p>
<p>The nearest <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a> weather station is in <a href="/wiki/Woburn,_Bedfordshire" title="Woburn, Bedfordshire">Woburn</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> located just outside the south eastern fringe of the Milton Keynes urban area.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milton_Keynes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although Milton Keynes was <a href="/wiki/History_of_Milton_Keynes#Milton_Keynes_Development_Corporation:_designing_a_city_for_250.2C000_people" title="History of Milton Keynes">specified to be a city in scale</a> and the term "city" is used locally (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter_alia" title="Inter alia">inter alia</a></i> to avoid confusion with its constituent towns), formally this title cannot be used. This is because conferment of <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status in the United Kingdom</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Royal_prerogative" title="Royal prerogative">Royal prerogative</a>.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
